Current Commentary

Strictly Prevent Cholera

— Ting

The weather is extremely hot this summer. The Yangtze River basin and the provinces of Henan and Shandong have been suffering from prolonged drought, and epidemics are spreading, creating many dangers. Take cholera, for example, which has always been a prevalent disease in our country during the summer, but the cyclical nature of its intense outbreaks is unpredictable. Therefore, during the summer, preventive measures must not be delayed and must not be relaxed on the grounds that there were few cases of true cholera last year.

Just three years ago, cholera was prevalent in twenty provinces and cities in our country, with 100,000 cases and more than 30,000 deaths. The severity of the disaster can be imagined. The fact that we were spared a true cholera outbreak last year may only be because it was in a passive latent state of a dormant cycle. To say that it will certainly not occur this year is too optimistic. According to the first announcement of the Shanghai Cholera Prevention Temporary Office, "Cholera vibrios with weak agglutinative properties were found three times in the river and pond water samples taken in May and June this year. This is very important for the study of cholera epidemics." News reports from Xuzhou indicate that the tiger plague is rampant, with deaths occurring every day, and coffin shops are unable to meet the demand. If it is not quickly suppressed and spreads to other places, the consequences will be dire.

According to experts, cholera generally spreads in two ways: one is explosive, caused by drinking water contaminated with bacteria, and the other is prolonged, transmitted by mosquitoes and flies coming into contact with bacteria. We are fortunate to live in large cities with tap water for drinking and vaccinations for protection. The chances of being infected are naturally not as high as in poor rural areas. On the other hand, the poor and suffering people in the interior mostly live in thatched huts and shacks, where mosquitoes and flies congregate and live together. Moreover, the water they drink is mostly taken from wells, rivers, and ponds. Transmission is easy, and infection is common. Furthermore, the weather is extremely dry this year, and the rivers and wells are shallow and silty, with turbid water. Based on common sense, the growth of cholera bacteria should be even faster than usual. Therefore, preventive measures cannot be delayed.

Furthermore, in 1931 (of the Republic of China), the Yangtze River and Huai River Canal basins were flooded, and sporadic cholera cases were seen in the autumn of that year, continuing into the early spring of the following year. Fortunately, the Disaster Relief Committee's preventive measures were effective, and the damage was reduced. This year, the rivers in eastern Hebei and northern Hubei have risen sharply, and the danger is extreme. The tragedy of being submerged is almost unavoidable. According to our experience, epidemics always follow floods. Those who die from epidemics are often more numerous than those who die from drowning or starvation. The cholera situation in the disaster areas in the future is extremely worrying. It is hoped that those in charge of water conservancy and public health will make plans as soon as possible to prevent the spread. As for the northwestern provinces, the territory is vast, and transportation is obstructed. Whenever there is a severe drought, epidemics are rampant, and people and livestock die in large numbers. During the cholera epidemic of 1932 (of the Republic of China), the provinces of Shaanxi, Shanxi, Sichuan, and Suiyuan all used airplanes to transport large quantities of vaccines from Beiping and Shanghai for prevention. It is heard that in April of this year, the Central Health Administration planned to establish a Northwest Epidemic Prevention Office to handle work such as serum vaccines nearby. The drought this summer is unprecedented. The need for a Northwest Epidemic Prevention Office is even more urgent.

In recent years, although our country's public health事业 cannot be compared with those of the great powers, it has also made some progress. For example, the Municipal Health Bureau and the Seaport Quarantine Administration in this city are quite serious about epidemic prevention work and can be taken as examples. However, the health administration in various provinces in the interior is still immature, and the poor and suffering people are mostly clueless about methods to prevent cholera and other seasonal epidemics. Therefore, it depends on the central and local health administrators and social leaders to go deep into the people and work hard. We all know that to prevent cholera, we must pay attention to the cleanliness and epidemic prevention propaganda, the implementation of vaccine injections, the promotion of disinfection campaigns, and the establishment of isolation hospitals. However, if it is only limited to large cities or the upper classes, it is far from enough to be considered universal, and the essence of public health is lost. Therefore, the main object of a true public health事業 must be the lower classes of the people, and a popular method must be used to promote it extensively. Cholera is one of the most dangerous infectious diseases. When talking about the way to prevent it, one must start from within.

Central National Government: Reports on Two Memorial Weeks, Ju Zheng: The Five-Power Constitution and the New Life Movement, Shao Yuanchong: The Spirit of Nationalism

(Nanjing) The Central Government held the 193rd Memorial Week on the morning of the 16th. Central Committee members Ju Zheng, Chen Lifu, Li Ciwen, Wang Qi, Hong Ludong, Xiao Jishan, Xie Zuomin, Miao Peicheng, Liang Hancao, Ke Xinge, and all staff members, totaling approximately 600 people, attended. Ju Zheng presided over the meeting. Chen Lifu reported, stating that the Premier's creation of the Five-Power Constitution was derived from the path of human survival and evolution. It is the evolution of humanity for survival, passing through several stages to form the five functions of legislation, administration, judiciary, examination, and supervision, in order to maintain the entire social order. Therefore, the Five-Power Constitution not only establishes a system but also has the function of selecting and eliminating people through examination and supervision, which is more complete than the three-power system. In short, although the system is good, it still needs morality to maintain its foundation. Therefore, the promotion of the New Life Movement, advocating propriety, righteousness, integrity, and a sense of shame, is sufficient to remedy the shortcomings of the system. Currently, why are there shortcomings in the trial implementation of the five-power system? Most of them are due to unclear powers and functions, incomplete laws and regulations, and the gradual decline of morality. This is an inevitable phenomenon in the trial implementation process and does not mean that the Premier's Five-Power Constitution is imperfect. In short, we should urgently promote morality, because there is no political system that can be discussed without morality. After the speech, the meeting adjourned around 9 o'clock. (Central News Agency dispatch, 16th)

(Nanjing) The National Government held a Memorial Week on the morning of the 16th. Shao Yuanchong, Chen Shaokuan, Cao Haosen, Chen Xunyong, Lin Xiang, Lü Chao, Wei Huai, and other officials from various Yuan, ministries, and commissions, totaling more than 300 people, attended. Shao Yuanchong presided over the meeting, led the attendees in paying respects, and delivered a report, stating that in engaging in the work of national rejuvenation, we should deeply understand the spirit of the Premier's nationalism. Its positive manifestations should be to strive from the basic work of consolidating the national foundation, promoting the progress of national politics, society, and culture. To complete this task, we must base ourselves on the Premier's spirit of education to cultivate independent knowledge, develop special abilities, and shoulder the responsibility of rejuvenating the nation. Its negative manifestations should be to fight for national survival in times of national crisis and have the spirit of self-sacrifice for the sake of benevolence. At the same time, we should have full faith in the constructive ability and the spirit of great men manifested in all aspects of our country's struggle history, such as politics, military affairs, society, and culture, to encourage ourselves to build the foundation for rejuvenating the nation and complete the responsibility of rejuvenating the nation. (Central News Agency dispatch, 16th)

Japanese Navy Decides: Demands to Divide Control of the Pacific: Will Abolish the Washington and London Treaties: Expand the Navy and Increase Air Force: Seize Hegemony Over a 2,000-Nautical-Mile Radius Circle

(Tokyo) The naval authorities are actively preparing for next year's naval disarmament conference. The meeting of the naval leadership, which opened at 11:00 a.m. this morning, decided on the following fundamental principles:

(1) Demand the revision of the Washington and London Treaties to establish a naval disarmament treaty that can preserve peace in East Asia and satisfy the sense of national defense security.

(2) Based on the right to equal armaments, change the total tonnage system to a restriction system, determine its maximum limit, and the amount of each type of warship within its scope should be freely decided by the country.

(3) In addition to fully implementing the established replenishment plan in the first and second items, increase the air force and expand its content to seize the naval power within a 2,000-nautical-mile radius circle centered on the Japanese archipelago and strengthen the national defense of the north.

(4) If the above plans are determined and prepared, Japan can ensure national security at any time in the event of an unexpected incident. (Japanese United News Agency dispatch, 16th)

British and American Representatives: Draft a Joint Statement: Explaining the Reasons for Postponing the Naval Conference

(London) Davis and other members of the American naval delegation will return to New York on July 19th. The current stage of the British-American naval talks has ended. British and American representatives have drafted a joint statement explaining the reasons for postponing the continuation of the talks, which will probably be published tomorrow. It is reported that the postponement of the talks is because it is necessary to first inquire about Japan's views before continuing. (Reuters dispatch, 16th)

(London) The news that the preliminary negotiations for the naval conference would be postponed until October has been confirmed here. According to the Daily Telegraph, the lack of progress in the preliminary negotiations is one of the reasons for the postponement. The differences between Britain and the United States regarding the tonnage of battleships and cruisers are as great as before, and the differences between Britain and France regarding submarines are also deep. Davis and the American government are greatly disappointed with the lack of results in the negotiations and the delay in the arrival of the Japanese representatives, and the Japanese representatives only have one naval officer. The conflict of opinions between France and Italy is also one of the reasons for the postponement. (National News dispatch, 16th)

(London) The American delegation participating in the preliminary talks for the 1935 naval conference will depart for New York this Thursday. The preliminary naval talks have been postponed until October, apparently because the United States must wait for Britain to determine its action plan, and Britain's action plan must largely await talks with Italy and Japan's statement of its intentions to Britain before it can be determined. The instructions given to the American delegation are only to record and report to the government the proposals put forward by all parties. Without Britain's initiative, the American delegation cannot promote the progress of the negotiations. (Havas dispatch, 16th)

(Tokyo) According to a telegram from Ambassador Matsudaira in England to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, when negotiating with the United States, the British side put forward a concrete proposal, but Japan, the United States, and France were not prepared to propose countermeasures, and Japan and the United States did not agree with Britain on the date of the naval disarmament conference. Therefore, Davis, the American representative, is taking advantage of the summer vacation to return home once, resulting in the temporary suspension of the talks for next year's conference. Foreign Minister Simon of England, Ambassador Matsudaira of Japan, and representative Davis of the United States will meet on the 17th to mutually state the process of the talks and decide to suspend the talks before the end of October. The three countries will jointly issue a statement, which will be at 11:00 a.m. on the 17th in Japan. Foreign Minister Hirota immediately replied to Ambassador Matsudaira, saying that Japan was only involved in procedural issues at the preliminary talks and did not enter into substantive talks, so Colonel Iwashita, who was specially dispatched by the Navy, should arrive in England in September. There is no objection to suspending the talks before then. In addition, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs will issue a statement in Tokyo when the statement is issued in London and is currently in contact with the British side. (Electric News dispatch, 16th)

Admiral Osumi: Explains the Navy's Position: Will be Incorporated into the Okada Cabinet's Foreign Policy Statement

(Tokyo) The meeting of the highest-ranking officers of the Navy convened at 11:00 a.m. on the 16th at the Admiral's official residence. All relevant dignitaries, including General Fushimi, Chief of the Naval General Staff, attended. First, Admiral Osumi described the situation regarding his continued tenure. Then, he presented the Japanese Navy's original proposal for the naval disarmament conference and gave a detailed explanation. He also stated that the proposal should be incorporated into the Okada Cabinet's internal and external policy platform as soon as possible. Next, Bureau Chief Yoshida of the Naval Affairs Bureau reported on the progress of the London preliminary meeting and advocated upholding the Navy's established policy. (Japanese United News Agency dispatch, 16th)

(Tokyo) The meeting of the highest-ranking officers of the Japanese Navy, which decided on the Navy's attitude toward next year's naval disarmament conference, was held at the Admiral's official residence at 11:00 a.m. today. Generals Fushimi, Chief of the Naval General Staff, Admiral Osumi, Kato, Nomura, Kobayashi, Yamamoto, Nakamura, Suetsugu, Nagano, Takahashi, Fujita, and other senior naval leaders all attended. First, Admiral Osumi stated the circumstances of his continued tenure in the current cabinet. Then, he explained the opinions on the new cabinet's national policy requested by the government from the Navy, which were submitted to Prime Minister Okada as follows: (1) Strive to restore the right to self-defense in the naval disarmament conference and withdraw from unfavorable treaties. (2) Establish a policy toward Manchuria. (3) Entrust the Navy with ensuring the League of Nations mandate territories. (4) Implement the national defense replenishment plan with 1936 as the target. Afterwards, Bureau Chief Yoshida of the Naval Affairs Bureau reported on the progress of the preliminary talks at the naval disarmament conference. After earnest discussions, the results were based on the following fundamental naval principles: (1) Abolition of the ratio system for each type of warship. (2) Establishment of the right to national self-defense. (3) Establishment of a sense of national security. (4) Should withdraw from unfavorable treaties and revise existing treaties. (5) Strive to conclude reasonable treaties that prevent heavily armed countries from autonomously reducing attacks on others. The countermeasures for dealing with the naval disarmament conference were submitted to the government, and this point will be clearly indicated to the people, urging the government to implement the empire's claims with national unity. After unanimous agreement, the meeting adjourned at 1:20 p.m. The officers who came to Beijing are scheduled to return to their posts on the 17th. (Electric News dispatch, 16th)

Tokonami, the New Minister of Communications: Developing Aviation Plans: Totaling 3 Million Yuan

(Tokyo) In order to cope with the extraordinary situation, the new Minister of Communications, Tokonami Takejiro, plans to include in the next year's budget a sum for establishing a national aviation policy, totaling 3 million yuan. The plans for air transport connecting Taiwan, Fukuoka, Tokyo, and Sapporo, the Japanese South Seas air route, the aviation plan crossing the Sea of Japan via Korea to the capital of "Manchukuo", and the plan for constructing more than ten airfields for its ground facilities are also included. (Japanese United News Agency dispatch, 16th)

It was heard today that Soviet Russia is likely to apply for membership before the opening of the next League of Nations General Assembly. These negotiations are being handled by the government, not by the League of Nations, so the League of Nations does not know the date of Soviet Russia's application. (Reuters dispatch, 15th)

The Mexican chargé d'affaires in Warsaw officially notified Soviet Ambassador Davtyan that the Mexican government is willing to restore normal diplomatic relations with the Soviet Union. (TASS dispatch, 16th)

Eastern European Pact: Germany Tends to Oppose: Fears France and Russia Will Control European Affairs

(Berlin) The Eastern Locarno Pact, for which the British ambassador to Germany formally sought German consent on Friday, has now aroused opposition in areas familiar with its content, on the grounds that the conclusion of the pact is not only insufficient to prevent war, but also sufficient to promote it. The semi-official organ "Foreign Political Review" published an article today stating that the draft agreement drawn up by British Foreign Secretary Simon and French Foreign Minister Barthou is nothing less than a "completely military pact." The newspaper added, "The Eastern Locarno Pact does not aim to consult with each other to resolve armed conflict in the event of difficulties in the first chapter, but only promotes mutual assistance, which shows that the premise of the pact is military in nature, which is enough to cause the world to be shocked and thoughtful. Moreover, there are many conflicts between the Eastern Locarno Pact and the League of Nations Covenant, because the League of Nations Covenant is a guarantee of peace, but now it is replaced by France's military alliance in Eastern Europe, which is sufficient to promote rapid and effective action. Once an accident occurs in the future, France can determine right and wrong and handle everything on its own. Then various newly concluded guarantee covenants can be destroyed at will, and the so-called peaceful reconciliation without resorting to force will be more difficult to follow in the future. Even the little ability left in the League of Nations Council today will be deprived of it in the future, and there will be no possibility of existence even in ideals. It is difficult for Germany to return to Geneva, where there is no guarantee of equal treatment, in such a settlement that promotes war. Moreover, the so-called issue of League of Nations reform seems to be a thing of the past in the eyes of the initiators of the Eastern Locarno Pact, and the League of Nations thereafter will also become a mere appendage under the control of French hegemony. But this is not just empty talk. It can be seen that it is not wrong to use recent events as evidence. The accession of Soviet Russia to the League of Nations is a one-handed affair of the three powers. No meetings were convened to discuss it in advance, nor was the consent of other member states sought, because they knew in advance that other countries would oppose it. However, since they are all member states, they should at least be given the opportunity to speak. Therefore, in the future, whenever any important event occurs in Europe, it can be handled by France and Russia in consultation. Therefore, this kind of policy is no longer an organized evolution, but only knows how to use political and military actions to create various "faits accomplis." (National News dispatch, 15th)

Wheat Crop Failure: US to Change Control Measures

(Washington) Following today's predictions of a poor grain harvest, the United States may abandon restrictions on grain production next year. According to experienced observers here, cotton and wheat have been severely affected by drought. It is unlikely that there will be further reductions in cultivated land. The predicted surplus of cotton and wheat will fall below the warning line. The Agricultural Adjustment Administration (AAA) believes that the emergency period for restricting grain is coming to an end. It may then adjust the production of flour and cotton. Agriculture Secretary Wallace stated that if the grain harvest is as poor as expected, wheat production will no longer be restricted next year. The AAA may allow for increased acreage. It is reported that the government is currently studying how many acres of land should be restored to cultivation so as not to hinder rising prices and the AAA's grain restriction program. It seems certain that there will be no need to control livestock production next year. The drought has greatly reduced forage, which will naturally limit livestock production. Since the AAA's cotton acreage restriction fell short of its target by one million bales, Congress passed the revolutionary Bankhead Act, imposing a cotton tax on excess imports to limit cotton production to ten million bales. For nearly a century, American domestic and foreign policies have been influenced by wheat production. Wheat production is also a litmus test for the New Deal's economic theories of production control and farmer cooperation. The government hopes to cooperate with other countries to restrict wheat production under the London Agreement by limiting acreage, and to subsidize exporters to develop markets across the Pacific. This trend towards national self-sufficiency has been accepted by farmers cultivating 77% of the land. 550,000 farmers have signed contracts, abandoning 7,595,000 acres. American taxpayers have also paid millions in taxes for the grain restriction program to subsidize farmers. (15th National Telegram)

Anti-Jewish Sentiment in Turkey

After investigating the alleged abuse of Jews in Selanik, the Istanbul Ministry of Interior today released a report stating that since the outbreak of anti-Jewish sentiment, 13,000 Jews have fled, with 3,000 leaving. The worst affected area was Koklariya, where the 65 Jewish households were looted by mobs. (15th Reuters Telegram)

Italian Ship Recovers 12,000 Gold Bars and £135,000 in Gold Coins

The Italian ships Artiglio and Rialto, which have been salvaging gold and silver from the British company's mail ship Egypt, which sank in 1922, have recovered 12,000 gold bars, £135,000 in gold coins, and 40 tons of silver. The ship has now returned here loaded with grain. According to today's news, the divers found the gold and silver storage of the Egypt to be empty. After checking the amount of gold and silver carried by the Egypt on the day of the sinking, it is believed that there are still 150 gold bars and 30 silver bars on the ship, possibly fallen into the cargo hold. Therefore, it is planned to drill through the cargo hold to find them. (15th Reuters Telegram)

Belgian and American Scientists to Probe the Stratosphere

Professor Cosyns of Brussels and a 23-year-old student of Professor Piccard are waiting for good weather in Ardennes to ascend into the stratosphere in a balloon. It is scheduled to begin around 4:00 AM this morning and remain airborne for about 10 to 15 hours. The purpose of this ascent is purely for scientific research on cosmic rays and is not intended to break any altitude records. (15th Reuters Telegram)

Latte's new stratosphere exploration plan was completed today. It is hoped that next week's weather will allow the world's largest balloon, sponsored by the National Geographic Society and the US Army Air Corps, to ascend into space according to the original detailed plan, in order to reach a distance of 16 miles above the ground. The balloon has a volume of three million cubic feet and can carry about one ton of scientific instruments. All instruments for recording scientific data are manufactured by the Wright-Fairfield Air Corps factory and laboratory, under the direction of Colonel Stevens. Colonel Stevens is skilled in aerial photography, so cameras are very important for reconnaissance recording and saving high-altitude scientific research work. (15th National Telegram)

Silver Prices and China

(London) Wilkins, chairman of the Currency Policy Committee of the British Textile Manufacturers Association, wrote to the Manchester Guardian today, denying the claim that high silver prices cause prices in China to fall. He said that after silver prices rise, the rest of the world will prosper, and the demand for Chinese specialties such as silk and tea will also increase. In 1924, when the price of silver was 34 pence per ounce, Lancashire sold 293 million square yards of cloth to China. In 1931, when the price of silver fell to 13 pence per ounce, Lancashire's cloth sales to China decreased to 81 million square yards. The following year, 1932, when the price of silver was 18 pence per ounce, China purchased 125 million square yards of cloth from Lancashire. (16th Reuters Telegram)

Vienna in Darkness for Several Hours

Vienna, the capital of Austria, was plunged into darkness for several hours this morning due to some bizarre act of revenge, with electricity, radio, telephone, and streetcars all shut down. It is widely believed that this was an action by the Communists to commemorate the seventh anniversary of the arson of the Vienna Palace of Justice. At midnight, Vienna's streetcars, suddenly encountering a world of darkness, were cut off from electricity and stopped on the tracks. All radio and broadcasting stations were silent. Most police stations were isolated due to telephone outages. After radio was restored this morning, the official explanation was that the main lines to Vienna were broken at the same time as a high-voltage power line outside the city was cut. Today, explosions occurred at the Central and Continental Hotels here, so the public believes that political action has not subsided. (16th National Telegram)

The Vienna Communist Party held a secret meeting in the Gartenless Forest to commemorate the seventh anniversary of the arson of the Vienna Palace of Justice. More than 1,000 people participated. Police and internal guards attempted to disperse the Communists. The Communists resisted strongly. Finally, the police opened fire several times, resulting in three deaths and twelve injuries. By the time reinforcements arrived, the Communists had dispersed, and only one leader was arrested. (16th National Telegram)

General Strike in San Francisco: Approximately 35,000 Workers on Strike; About 1.5 Million People Affected; The Second General Strike in American History

The general strike in San Francisco began at 8:00 AM this morning. Yesterday, striking workers rioted after looting food stores, resulting in troops using bayonets to kill one striking worker. The Washington government is constantly exchanging information with San Francisco and communicating with President Roosevelt by radio. Police and the National Guard have increased their defenses. The Federal Second Army is stationed locally, and if the California troops are insufficient, the Federal troops will maintain order. (16th Havas Telegram)

San Francisco began a general strike here at 8:00 AM this morning. This is the first time a general strike has been held in the United States. The strike workers' steering committee made the final preparations last night and decided on the following measures: (1) Food and gasoline in the city will be sold on a limited basis with coupons. (2) Organize "union police" in accordance with discipline to work with regular police to prevent violence. (3) Try to get all non-union workers, about 50,000, to join the strike. (4) The union authorities have designated 17 restaurants as public dining places. (5) Many companies have reserved entire floors of rooms in nearby hotels so that employees who cannot return home due to the public transport strike can stay temporarily in the hotels. In addition, strike pickets are blocking trucks carrying food into the city outside the city and prohibiting violence. There is a growing sense of food shortage in the city. California Governor Merriam has transferred 2,000 National Guard troops to San Francisco and declared that he will use troops to protect trucks carrying food into the city. The entire city is virtually under martial law. Washington has declared that the government will not interfere in the strike unless ordered by President Roosevelt. (16th Havas Telegram)

San Francisco is in a state of tension. The second general strike in history is scheduled to begin at 10:00 AM this morning. It is estimated that more than 1.5 million people will be affected. Two thousand defense troops from California are now heading to the port area from their camp 250 miles south of here, so it is rumored today that martial law will be declared. The defense troops are under secret orders to rush south with their equipment, hoping to arrive here by 10:00 AM. It is estimated that between 30,000 and 45,000 workers went on strike on Monday, and other workers will join the strike in the next few days. Several thousand others will have to strike due to the shutdown of most industries and the lack of transportation. Senior executives and other non-union members are in a very difficult situation. If they move to hotels near their offices, they will have no food. If they stay at home, they will not be able to work. By Wednesday, 150,000 people may be on strike. Grocery companies and retailers will all be shut down due to traffic disruption. Businessmen's losses will be millions of dollars a day. Negotiations between the Waterfront Employers Association, dockworkers, and sailors have been ineffective. The desolation and desolation of the streets of San Francisco is unprecedented in the city's history. Occasionally, a car speeds past on the streets, attracting attention and private discussions about where the gasoline came from. Streetcar and railway transportation will be completely shut down at 10:00 AM. A special gas station is open as usual. Doctors can purchase gasoline here with special permission. Grocery stores are still open on Sundays, which is the last chance for residents to buy food, but when they close, there are few canned goods left on the shelves. Governor Merlin has ordered patrol teams to drive trucks to various parts of the port, but few vehicles have arrived. Most housewives are stocking up on food in preparation for a long-term siege. Although the union allows special transportation for hospitals and health departments, most of the elderly and infants are inconvenienced by the lack of fuel and hot water in homes, hotels, and apartments. Fresh meat is no longer available due to the butcher's strike, and there is no source of fresh eggs. Fresh milk for babies is only available at hospitals and farms ten to fifteen miles away. Vegetable prices are soaring, and prices of all items are skyrocketing. The theater workers' union will also join the strike this morning, so all industries will be shut down. The state government's troops and police officers are patrolling the key coastal areas of San Francisco, but no riots have occurred on Sunday. The labor unrest has not yet been resolved. The whole city is filled with an unnatural atmosphere of desolation, as the residents of the metropolis are anxiously awaiting future developments. The general strike in eastern San Francisco, originally scheduled to take place on Tuesday morning, will cause cities such as Akron, Hickley, Haywood, Abenai, and others to become dead cities like San Francisco after 10:00 AM this morning. The printing industry union strike has been avoided, otherwise it will cause newspapers to temporarily suspend publication. (16th National Telegram)

After a period of quiet in the San Francisco labor unrest, riots broke out on the riverfront again today. Mobs used trucks as cover to throw stones at soldiers and police. Although they were driven away, they did not disperse. The soldiers and police then opened fire, resulting in several deaths and injuries. One person attempted to seize a soldier's rifle and was stabbed with a bayonet. At the same time, police patrol cars rushed to various places to provide assistance and were very busy. A total of ten strikers were arrested. In Oakland, mobs smashed the glass windows of food stores and looted. Many stores were closed for fear of being looted and did not do business. The general strike in San Francisco tomorrow, which will involve 150,000 workers, is scheduled to begin at 8:00 AM tomorrow morning. The central army will maintain order in the city when the strike is realized. San Francisco Mayor Rossi said to the public today that he would put down the strike and said that there were extremists in it who were determined to revolt. The police chief has recruited 500 special armed police officers and a cavalry squad. President Roosevelt is paying close attention to this matter. If the situation becomes too serious, the President may shorten his trip. Residents rushed to purchase food and other items to obtain sufficient supplies, so that the inventories of many stores were sold out today. Some stores are now limiting the quantity that customers can purchase. Many restaurants have closed their doors because they cannot obtain supplies. The strike committee today asked the strikers not to interfere with the supply of milk, bread, meat, etc. needed by hospitals, so hospitals can be unaffected by the general strike. The largest force of dockworkers is now concentrated in the port, wanting to gain control of the port's employment. Most local newspapers oppose the strike. The dockworkers' demands are: (1) Recognition of the union as an employment management agency. (2) A 30-hour work week. (3) $1 per hour wage. (4) Overtime pay of $1.50 per hour. (15th Reuters Telegram)

In Houston today, dockworkers on strike and non-striking workers clashed on a ship in the port. Gunshots were fired, resulting in the deaths of three non-union black dockworkers on the spot. One other person was seriously injured. In addition, two non-union black dockworkers and one white dockworker belonging to the union were slightly injured. (15th Reuters Telegram)

(2) Even if the current officials have been suspended from their positions, they should still only re-elect half of the officials according to law. The other people cooling off responded in unison, swarming into the park, smashing doors, windows, and equipment, and piling up rattan chairs and other items, setting them on fire, resulting in significant losses. The fire was still not extinguished by 12:00 AM. Wu Xisheng, the police officer of the 2nd district, was also beaten during the incident. (16th Special Dispatch)

Tang Youren, Under Wang Jingwei's Orders, Urges Huang Fu to Return North. Yin Tong, Persuaded by Huang, May Withdraw His Resignation.

Hangzhou News: Tang Youren, Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs, arrived in Mogan Mountain by car via the Jing-Hang (Nanjing-Hangzhou) National Highway on the evening of the 13th. He switched to a rattan sedan chair to ascend the mountain, carrying Premier Wang Jingwei's order to visit Huang Yingbai at his private residence at number 509. Later, Yin Tong also arrived, and they engaged in secret talks until after 11:00 PM. Tang and Yin returned to the Railway Hotel together, with Tang staying in room 116. At 7:20 AM on the 14th, Huang Fu went to the Mogan Mountain Public Welfare Association to handle association affairs in his own rattan sedan chair and then visited Tang at the Railway Hotel. They talked until 11:00 AM and then went to Huang's residence for lunch. After lunch, they had further lengthy discussions. Tang and Yin left Huang's residence at 9:30 PM to return to their lodgings to rest. When reporters visited, Tang stated that the reasons for Huang's delay in going north were: (1) the weather was too hot; (2) the North China issue had been largely resolved after the traffic problem was addressed, so Huang was staying in the mountains to avoid the heat. As a result of my (Tang referring to himself) meeting with Huang, Premier Wang hopes that he will return to the north as soon as possible to preside over the North China political situation. Huang intends to go after the weather cools down, so it is impossible to force him. The date of his departure from the mountain is uncertain. The entire North China issue should return to a normal diplomatic and ordinary political state as soon as possible; otherwise, we feel pain, and they are constantly suspicious, which is detrimental to both sides internationally. The withdrawal of Japanese troops from the war zone and other issues are not as serious as the rumors suggest and need to be referred to Chairman Huang for handling, which Huang can resolve after going north. Abolishing the Tanggu Truce is not an easy matter, and the central government has not yet discussed it. The rumor that negotiations will begin at the beginning of next month is probably not true. Chairman He (Jian) has returned from the southwest, and the leaders of the southwest have a better understanding of the central government's military and political aspects. Yin Tong's resignation, after Huang's personal persuasion, will return to the north in the coming days and may withdraw his resignation. Tang went down the mountain at 5:00 AM this morning (15th), took a car back to Hangzhou, and returned to Nanjing to report. (15th)

Xiamen Taiwanese Residents' General Assembly. This Year Has Seen a Large Increase in Taiwanese Coming to Xiamen. Japanese Business Has Also Seen a Rapid Advance.

Xiamen Correspondent: The Xiamen Taiwanese Association is organized by Taiwanese Japanese residents. Its scope was expanded last year, and it holds a general assembly (members' meeting) once a year. This year's second general assembly was held on July 8th. Those present that day included Tsukamoto Takeshi, the Japanese Consul stationed in Xiamen; Suigen Tsunehachi, the Deputy Consul of Justice; Ogawa Kaname, the Chief of the Japanese Police Station; Kato, the Director of the Xiamen Branch (Japanese people set up a police branch in Xiamen without authorization, exercising police power over residents, which has no basis in the treaty and has not been revoked despite repeated protests from our side); Sano, the patrol chief; and consular staff detectives. In addition, there were Japanese resident members, Taiwanese association members, and so-called committee members from the various Taiwanese districts in Xiamen. During the meeting, Shoji, the Japanese principal of the Asahi Ei School in Xiamen, reported on the teaching facilities of the Asahi Ei School, stating that the school had 602 students, including 348 boys and 254 girls, all taught in Japanese, with instruction in loyalty to the emperor and love of country (the Japanese Empire). Shoji also stated that, of these 602 students, about 150 were Chinese children, in addition to Taiwanese Japanese residents. Shoji also said that the Chinese students in the class would benefit the Taiwanese people in Xiamen in the future. Tsukamoto Takeshi then gave a speech, stating that last year, due to repeated political changes in the local area, they focused on foreign affairs and had no time to take care of internal affairs. Now that foreign affairs are in the past, they will focus on organizing internal affairs. According to the association's report on the economic situation, last year's income included 9,900 yuan in membership fees, 6,064 yuan in foreign firm fees, 3,666 yuan in clerical fees and guarantee handling fees, and 10,402 yuan in public security maintenance fees (this item is the 1,000 yuan per month that the Taiwanese Association pays to our Public Security Bureau to offset the police tax for Taiwanese residents. Therefore, all residents

shops, households, and stores with registered signs in Xiamen do not pay police taxes, resulting in a huge loss to the Public Security Bureau). This year's budget has increased membership fees to 27,108 yuan, an increase of 19,608 yuan, a two-fold increase, indicating the large number of Taiwanese people newly arriving in Xiamen. Foreign firm assessment fees have also increased to 11,350 yuan, an increase of 6,000 yuan over last year, also a two-fold increase, indicating the rapid progress of Japanese business in Xiamen recently. On the expenditure side, the original education fee for the Asahi Ei School of 5,000 yuan has been increased to 7,000 yuan, and there are two new expenses: (1) District security affairs fee (according to Taiwanese people, this year, in Xiamen, autonomous district security is established according to the areas of streets and villages without the permission of our official authorities. The current form is in opposition to our autonomous district security associations); (2) Confidential fee. It is unknown what the so-called confidential matters are. (July 13th)

National Army Advances on Shicheng and Ningdu in Three Routes. Baishui Has Been Captured, and Shicheng Is Being Attacked from Yiqian.

Nanchang Correspondent: It was recently learned from Guangchang that when the three-route army advanced south towards Baishui Town, 40 li from the city, the □□□ division came into contact with bandits. If this step is taken, the pseudo-central government will disintegrate. (July 15th)

Inspection Notes from the Northwest: Relics of Natural and Man-made Disasters. Special Correspondent for This Newspaper: Geng Ya

On the 29th at dawn, we departed from Chang Liushui. The wheels of the car became mired in the sand at Shawo (commonly known as the Dead Baby Pit), even more so than yesterday. When the wheel was lifted, the sand flowed down like water being poured from a waterwheel. We made a sloping path up to reduce the weight of the car and agreed to walk. After 30 li, we reached the top of the slope. There was a temple called Doumu Gong. We rested for two hours before the horse-drawn carriage arrived. After strong winds, stone rods often appear in the sand pits nearby, shaped like winding, broken snakes. The villagers call them "earth dragon bones" and say they can cure male hernias and irregular menstruation in women. The temple master sells them for a good profit. Upon examining them, their shape and texture were like animal bones, and their color was similar to lime, but they were very hard and had fine holes in them. I suspect that they were fossilized bones. The claim that they "cure diseases like magic" is just a false statement by the temple master to collect money. The palace was built in the twelfth year of the Qing Yongzheng era by the Zhongwei Diaoshapo Tea Society. It was repaired once by Ji Hongchang's troops and is still brand new today. Travelers rarely see springs for dozens of miles. After drinking here, everyone felt revitalized and grateful for the kindness. There is also no water in the temple, so they have to transport it back and forth, a journey of 40 li in total. It is said that when the Qinghai army passed the temple on its way to aid Ningxia, the locals used 30 donkeys to transport water for drinking and forbade cooking and watering horses, yet still several donkeys died from exhaustion. This shows how precious water is.

After traveling another ten or so li, we arrived at Yishaoquan (One Spoon Spring) and stayed there. The wounded soldiers from Qinghai who had stayed here last night had not yet left. They were leaning on crutches, bandaged, crawling on their knees, each in a different state, all heartbreaking to see. They were being transported by camel teams, traveling at night and resting during the day, making it even more inconvenient. The weather was hot, and all the camel hair had fallen off, making them difficult to look at. There were only three families of residents, who had repeatedly suffered from the disasters of war and said that they would move to another place. The leaking rooms and broken sheds were all occupied by wounded soldiers, so we temporarily sat on stone piers in front of the door. Suddenly, we heard a soft sobbing sound. We saw a young orderly, ordered by the medical officer to find water, who had failed and been whipped, breaking his right arm, with blood flowing profusely, soaking his sleeve. The orderly was from Henan and was 14 years old. His father had died in military service in 1918, and his mother had remarried. At that time, he was nine years old. He joined the 15th Route Army and attended the disaster relief school in Luoyang. Later, he moved with the army to Ningxia. This spring, when Sun Dianying's army invaded the west, Ningxia province expanded the hospital's staff of wounded soldiers. The disaster relief school was dissolved, and the students had nowhere to go, so they were assigned to various hospitals. The younger ones were used as orderlies, and the older ones as medics. Later, when the wounded soldiers' hospital closed, the orphans lost their homes again. The orderly had no place to rely on. He followed the wounded soldiers of the Qing army returning to Qinghai but was unexpectedly injured along the way, which was very painful. As the orderly spoke, tears kept falling. Suddenly, a military officer arrived, and the orderly quickly wiped away his tears with his left palm and gave a standing salute. The officer seemed surprised that he did not raise his hand, glanced at him askance, and passed by. Many who heard this found the medical officer's cruelty strange, but how could they know that the poison of war was the cause of this? Since he was already the wife of a widower and the son of an orphan, and society was not a healthy organization, there was no way to educate and support these helpless people. Only then did we discover that similar or even worse situations existed. Is this really the fault of the medical officer alone?

Swift Yellow Goats (also known as Wild Goats)

The three families of residents at Yishao Spring all run inns. We initially stayed temporarily at the west store. At 4:00 PM, the wounded soldiers set off. The east store was cleaner, so we moved there. However, the owner of the west store, with a head wrapped in mourning cloth, confronted the owner of the east store, questioning him in vulgar language and spitting everywhere, which was unbearable to witness. Later, Su Yuanzhang's soldiers, through various persuasions and slightly threatening words, finally made her weep and leave. According to the two store owners, they were originally from the same family, but due to competition for livelihood, they did not hesitate to stage this tragedy. The power of economic magic is so great. This is also a necessary product of modern society.

We departed from Yishao Spring on the 30th, traveling with Mr. Xu. The road was still sandy, but flatter. After 30 li, we reached Gantangzi, with only two or three courtyards of empty houses remaining. There was no sign of life, only several barn owls standing still on the rooftops and a flock of gray pigeons in the courtyard. The pigeons flew away when people arrived. Mr. Xu suddenly saw a small yellow goat and was startled into a earth bed, where it was captured by smoke. It was a wild hare. There were dozens of buried vats in the house, which were said to be for storing water. Shortly after, Mr. Du and Mr. Luo arrived by car. They immediately took out dry steamed buns to eat, and each person drank a cup of tea, because the water source was 20 li away, and there was no way to fetch water.

We continued past Jianhou for 60 li to Yingpanshui. In the distance, we saw several broken houses and wondered if anyone lived there. There was a Guandi Temple east of the village, but the main hall was empty, and the pillars and rafters of the two corridors had also been dismantled. The ground was covered with tiles, so we suspected that no one lived there. Suddenly, we smelled the scent of opium coming faintly from the village house. Upon closer inspection, a woman with disheveled hair was smoking and enjoying herself. In the courtyard, a pile of horse manure had accumulated, and several piglets were fighting over a lamb fetus, with blood and flesh scattered everywhere. We went to another house, where the roof was riddled with holes and the tiles and rafters had been removed, leaving only four walls. We asked, and they said that the large army had taken them for fuel when passing through, and they had to sleep in the open. West of the village stood rows of tombstones, mostly with inscriptions such as "Military Cavalry Colonel" and "Chengde Lang" from the previous Qing dynasty, indicating that the villagers were still descendants of officials.

However, they have declined to this point because they do not engage in farming and are harmed by opium. Most of the villagers make a living by finding black moss, collecting half a catty to a catty per day, earning an average of 30 cents, but only for a few months of the year, which is not a long-term source of income. The method of collecting black moss is to use an iron rake to scrape it from the ground. It is most abundant in March, April, July, and August, and less abundant in May and June. If there is too much rain, it is difficult to rake up, and if there is too little rain, it will not grow. There were many buyers in previous years, and the price rose to 1.20 yuan per catty. Now, it is three catties per yuan, and it is impossible to sell. The lives of the villagers are becoming increasingly difficult. Black moss is used as a cold dish at the opening of businesses and banquets, because the sound of its name is the same as "get rich."

The lives of the villagers in that area are very difficult, so the customs have declined, and the women have become addicted to opium, so their behavior is often unruly. The place where we stayed was a relatively clean room. The furnishings were clear at a glance, including a dirt stove, a pile of fuel, a pair of sand vats, with several rolls of black moss placed in the middle, and no food for rats to eat. There was a broken dirt bed with two broken burlap bags and three small yellow sheepskins, which were the bedding for the residents. There was nothing else. The resident gave the bed to the guests and slept on the ground, which was very uncomfortable. On the 31st, we went out at dawn. The road was muddy, and the mountain torrents were raging. Only then did we know that it had rained heavily last night, but we had not heard the sound of rain because the earthen house had no tiles. The car could not travel, so we stayed where we had slept last night. We bought a beam of wood for 30 cents and broke it with stones to cook rice for lunch. In the afternoon, we chatted and said that such villages were like tribes from the primitive era, or even worse. Primitive people could dig holes and build forests to live in and hunt animals for food, but the villagers here could not get meat. The earthen houses could not withstand wind and rain and were not as comfortable as the cave dwellings and forest dwellings of primitive people. The host heard this and sighed, "I am from Dajin County. I originally had hundreds of acres of good land, and hundreds of households lived there, with a population of nearly a thousand people. Unfortunately, in 1918, there was a drought in the Northwest. I had no way to make a living, so I led my wife and children to flee here, eating wild vegetables every day, drinking cold water, and living in earthen caves. The living conditions at that time were a hundred times worse than they are now. Dajin has now returned to its original state. If I had the travel expenses, I would return home." We continued to inquire and learned that his wife was from a Confucian family and had three sisters. She was the second, named Ergu, who was intelligent and knew a few words, and was praised by the villagers. Unfortunately, her life was unfortunate. She had just married a farmer when she suffered a drought. Her eldest sister and third sister married officials and merchants, respectively, and were well-fed, but they were stingy and unwilling to help her. She also had a weak younger brother, who also fled due to the drought and was abandoned by her eldest sister and third sister. She alone comforted and retained him, and now he has grown up and can help with the work. When Ergu talked about her life, her demeanor was quite dignified. In the past, the stations near Yingpanshui were prosperous areas along the Gansu-Ningxia post road. There were merchants opening stores, people digging coal and salt mines, and people farming or picking mountain vegetables, all of whom could support themselves and make a living. Now, the population is sparse, and the houses are dilapidated. Places such as Gantangzi and Qingyajie have completely become ruins, with no sign of life, and the scenery is desolate, as if one is in the realm of ghosts. Alas, the cruelty of natural and man-made disasters!

Hebei Province to Abolish Excessive Taxes in Stages. The First Phase Will Be Implemented in Mid-July. A Total of 1.24 Million Taxes Will Be Cut.

Tianjin News: The Hebei Provincial Government previously passed the abolition of surcharges on land taxes and excessive miscellaneous taxes at its 524th meeting. Following the resolution of the Central Financial Conference, the Financial Department will implement the abolition in stages starting from July 1, the 23rd year of the Republic. The Financial Department will also select 47 counties from the province's 131 counties, based on the severity of the excessive taxes, and include them in the first phase. In these 47 counties, the land tax exceeds three times the amount of the original tax, and there are as many as 11 types of excessive taxes. It is estimated that the total amount of excessive taxes abolished in the first phase is 550,000 yuan. The land tax surcharges in 32 counties, including Cangxian, will be reduced by a total of 790,000 yuan. The total amount of taxes abolished in the two areas is 1.24 million yuan. The original date for implementation was July 1, but it was postponed to July 20 due to the unsettled compensatory measures and the inability of the counties to complete the preparations in time. However, the starting date is still July 1. The Financial Department is also planning the second phase, which will abolish a total of more than 1.1 million yuan in taxes. The third and fourth phases of the abolition will continue in turn. By the end of this year, the province will completely abolish the taxes according to the date determined by the National Financial Conference. There are two compensatory measures for the tax cuts: one is that 10% of the revenue from the tobacco and alcohol license tax collected by the province will be used, and the other is to carry out land reporting. The province's stamp tax collects a total of more than one million yuan per year. The province will take 10%, and the counties will take 30%. The province can use only 400,000 yuan for compensation. The license tax can collect 500,000 yuan per year, totaling less than 900,000 yuan, which is not enough to compensate for the amount of the first phase of the tax cuts. The compensation for the third and fourth phases is even more hopeless. Therefore, the Financial Department has decided to carry out land reporting at the same time to increase revenue. As for the tobacco and alcohol license tax, after the Ministry ordered that it be transferred to the province for collection on July 1, the Financial Department has submitted a request to the Provincial Government that the tax collection bureaus in the province and cities collect it on behalf of the province. Counties without tax collection bureaus will contract the tax collection to merchants, following the example of the tax on brokers. Separate methods for tax collection bureaus to collect on behalf of the province and counties to contract to merchants will be drafted separately and submitted to the Ministry for approval. However, the old Tobacco and Alcohol Bureau has reported to the Ministry that all the tobacco and alcohol licenses have been cancelled after the handover. Therefore, the Financial Department has sent a special telegram to the Ministry to issue another 100,000 licenses so that they can be collected within this month. The county governments have been ordered to determine the standard price according to the proportion of the tobacco and alcohol tax bureau's collection of license fees in their respective counties and to solicit bids from merchants within ten days so that the collection can begin immediately after the licenses are received. (13th)

Forty People Die of Heatstroke in Jinan. ▲Crops Wither and Drought Conditions Appear.

Jinan Correspondent: Since the beginning of summer, the weather in this city has been dry, with little rainfall, and drought conditions have gradually appeared. Since the rainfall on the 3rd, the heat has increased day by day. Yesterday (14th), the indoor temperature reached 100 degrees Fahrenheit, and the outdoor temperature reached 125 degrees. There have been reports of people dying from heatstroke every day for the past three days. According to reports yesterday, as many as 40 people died. The number of people who were treated and recovered is difficult to count. Even a mule died of heatstroke. The asphalt roads in the city melted, and pedestrians walked as if they were walking on cotton. The autumn crops in the suburbs were also mostly damaged by drought. It is said that if there is no rain for another three days, the autumn harvest will be hopeless. It is estimated that the people who died of heatstroke included a woman south of Gan Shi Qiao, two people near Lude Hospital, one person in Anpingli, an old woman south of Tianqiao, three people in the Anhui Yidi, one man and one woman on Weiyi Road, a Feng student in Shunxing Yuan on Xiaowei Er Road, two water sellers named Guo and Zhou in Sanlizhuang, one person in Xishunju at the north end of Buzhengsi Street, one person in Sanyilou on Bianzhi Lane, one child in Beiyuan, two people on Anchasisi Street, one person on Xianqian Street, one person on Nanbeicang Lane, one person in Guanyuan, one person outside the South Gate, one person on Songlin Street, two people in Majialinzi, one person at the south entrance of Xinshichang, five people in front of Paotouquan, and eight people in the vicinity of Jindehui. A rickshaw puller suddenly fell to the ground and fainted at the south entrance of Weisan Road. Fortunately, a nearby hospital heard about it and immediately sent a doctor to see him. He still had a faint breath, so he was given a cardiotonic injection and was revived. There were also many reports of others whose lives were endangered by heatstroke. As for the exact number of deaths, I am afraid that it is more than that. (15th)

Guangdong Prohibits Articles on Men and Women Walking Together. ▲Regulations from the Provincial River Supervision and Distribution Bureau.

Guangzhou Correspondent: The Guangdong provincial authorities have spared no effort in criticizing fashionable actions and modern etiquette. Previously, Zhang Zhiying, the commander of the fleet, proposed to ban men and women from swimming together in the summer, which has already been implemented by the Public Security Bureau. Recently, Zheng Ridong, the director of the Provincial River Supervision and Distribution Bureau, has proposed to the government to prohibit men and women from walking arm in arm. The following is a transcription of Zheng's original proposal: "Since world civilization has been poured into China, European and American customs have rushed in. Guangdong was the first to open up and is afraid of falling behind. Women are liberated, and social interactions are public. Giving peonies and picking orchids

spreads scandalous rumors beyond the Wei River, while returning beauty and leaving pipes transmit romantic stories in the corners of the city. During this transition period, there may be acts of wantonness and transgression in the pursuit of the two sexes. Bystanders criticize and consider it a cause for concern about people's hearts and morals. Ideologies go to extremes, and opinions are difficult to integrate. The recent order issued by the government to ban men and women from swimming together has aroused social attention. The nature of the people is stubborn and aspires to be saints and sages. They hate the new trend and strongly advocate ancient etiquette. I believe that the mixture of swimming pools should be banned first, but the prevention of parading in the city should not be delayed. In the past, men went by the right and women went by the left, as seen in the articles of the Wang Zhi Dao Lu. "There are women in cars, and there are women walking together," which are the poems of Zheng and Wei about lustful runaway. Nowadays, as social customs are declining and people's morals are becoming more perverse, they compete to imitate the fashion and disregard etiquette. Beautiful women with golden hair often tread on the streets, and delicate figures in embroidered pavilions are accustomed to soaring on the roads. Applying rouge and powder serves as a target, while exposing arms and breasts is deliberately provocative. As a result, swarms of bees chase after them, delighted to share the beauty, and stray butterflies follow behind, hoping to sniff a trace of fragrance. The frivolous often go up and down, while the sincere also gallop their hearts. In chance encounters, they may form illicit relationships, and in the bustle, each boasts of their glamorous encounters. The way of shame is completely lost, and cases of adultery and abduction are increasing day by day. What will the end be? Now that the practice of swimming together has already been banned, but there has been no prevention of the harm of walking together. I suspect that the clear prohibition is stricter on water than on land. In the end, I am afraid that the bad customs cannot be quelled, and the root cannot be corrected and the source cleared. Every time one sets foot on the road, one sees strange sights: strange costumes and seductive clothes, flocks of women in groups, holding hands and side by side, loving couples. Passersby look sideways, and vulgar people are even more heartbroken. Thinking that bad habits should be eliminated together, sighing who will share the tide, I humbly offer a contribution of straws and chen, serving as a Chen of the tube leopard. I hope that it will be adopted and implemented, and the future of the party-state will be very fortunate!" (July 10th)

Songjiang: Disputes Between Songhui Garden and the Fire Brigade.

The weather has been very dry recently, and there has been no rain for a long time. The river water has dried up, and the fire brigades in the first district are practicing their operations and testing their machinery in order to prevent fire alarms. They have notified all members to drive their vehicles to the Songhui Automobile Road every afternoon at 6:00 PM to test the vehicles. There is the Songhui Amusement Park there, which is a place for the people of Song to cool off and relax. The road is blocked by the general public who go to the automobile road to take a walk and cool off. At about 7:00 PM last night, the gasoline lamp inside the gate of the amusement park suddenly caught fire. The fire brigade members, seeing the situation, feared that a small spark would cause a prairie fire. Being responsible, they immediately drove the car to pour water. The onlookers applauded, and the sound of people was boiling over. The more people gathered, the more people gathered. Suddenly, the belt was cut off, and a barrel of Hua An Long Gaisi Lin was knocked over, and the transmission line was burned. The fire brigade suffered a lot of losses. It is unknown how someone threw bricks and smashed the doors and windows of the amusement park, and the chartered car was also damaged. As a result, a dispute arose between the fire brigade and the Songhui Amusement Park. The fire brigade filed a complaint with County Magistrate Jin at 11:00 PM that night. This morning, the county party department convened representatives from local organizations and the fire brigade to mediate. It is heard that the county government representative gently advised the fire brigade to suspend the vehicle test for two days and wait for a solution. The fire brigade has agreed to accept it. How will it be resolved in the future? We will continue to explore and report.

Suzhou: Villagers Come to the City to Report Famine and Petition

Wu County has not had rain for over twenty days, and the drought is becoming apparent. Farmers from various villages are reporting the famine to the county government. More than 100 representatives, chosen by the farmers from 39 villages in Weiting, came to the city yesterday (the 16th) morning to petition the county government. Their purpose was twofold: (1) to request the opening of the Wangting Shadun harbor, (2) to request the allocation of twenty water-lifting machines. The Wu County Magistrate personally received them. Regarding the first point, according to the Construction Department's plan, water would be lifted into the Shadun harbor and introduced into the inland river. The Construction Department has commissioned Wang Yuanyuan to come to Suzhou immediately. Further discussions will be held upon his arrival in Suzhou. The second point must be submitted to the drought prevention conference on the 17th for comprehensive deliberation. The representatives left satisfied. It is also heard that the drought prevention committee has dispatched Committee Member Zhang Yunbo to Shanghai to purchase 43 water-lifting machines, which were transported to Suzhou yesterday (the 16th) in preparation for distribution to various villages for use.

Chamber of Commerce Convenes to Discuss Relief for People's Food

Chairman Shi of the County Chamber of Commerce, in view of the recent soaring rice prices and the difficult livelihood of the common people, specially convened rice industry representatives Xu Jusheng, Chen Junyu, Zhu Ren'an, Qian Lichun, and others at the Chamber of Commerce at 9:00 AM yesterday (the 16th) to discuss relief measures. Chairman Shi Yunqing decided on four principles: (1) The grain industry association will notify all members to cease supplying outside areas in order to provide relief locally. (2) The rice shop association will list and report the actual sales volume in the last ten days, as well as the actual number of existing stocks, for verification. (3) The price of ordinary indica rice is even more related to the staple food of the poor and should be reduced by both associations. (4) The government should be petitioned to temporarily cancel the import tax on foreign rice to increase supply. The Chamber of Commerce will notify the representatives of the two associations of the above four measures, convene a meeting, and submit a report on the handling of the matter within three days.

Wuxi: Trafficking Drug Pills Arrested and Sent to the County

Police officers from the Ninth Branch of the Public Security Bureau, earlier arrested Hu Litang in Rongxiang while carrying red pills. Three thousand red pills were confiscated and handed over to the main bureau for strict interrogation. According to his confession, the red pills belonged to Dong Bifu, a former guard in the Public Security Bureau, who instructed him to deliver them to a certain place. The Inspectorate dispatched Inspector Ge to arrest Dong Bifu and bring him to the bureau. Dong confessed to trafficking drug pills without hesitation. Yesterday (the 16th), both were sent to the county government for trial. In addition, the counties of Xiyi Lichang have long been places permeated with poisonous atmosphere. In addition to opium and morphine, Wuxi also has red, black, white, fast, and super-fast drug pills, which sell extremely well. It is heard that the manufacturers are Hu, Xiao, Xu, and others, who are making considerable profits.

Recently, he was plagued by poverty and illness, and seeing the crops withered and the autumn harvest hopeless, his livelihood became difficult to maintain. He secretly hanged himself a few days ago. It is indeed tragic.

Yangzhou is experiencing extreme heat and severe drought. An epidemic of acute infectious disease is prevalent. According to the report of the temple caretaker of the Prefectural Temple, the number of deaths in recent days (according to Yangzhou custom, when people die, they must go to the Prefectural Temple to offer incense, called "paving the hall") has been over a hundred, with the highest reaching 217 people.

Jiading: Elderly Female Farmers Go to the County to Protest Famine

Extreme heat and drought have created a famine. Farmers prayed to gods and Buddhas, but to no avail. The autumn harvest is about to be hopeless. On the morning of the 14th, fifty to sixty female farmers from Chuiyi Tu in Anqiao Township went to the county government to protest the famine, stating that there was no way to lift water, the rice fields had turned into scorched earth, rice prices were soaring, and life was difficult. They requested an on-site inspection and relief. The crowd was large and chaotic. Zhang Hailong, a staff member of the county government, represented Magistrate Xu and came out to comfort them, promising to find a way to provide relief and giving each person 60 cash for refreshments before they dispersed.

Jiashan: Key Suspects in the East Gate Bloodshed Case Arrested

Li Shijie and Xu Mingde, the key suspects in the violent assault and bloodshed case at the Risheng Lou on East Gate Street in this county, fled far away by boat with two rifles and one short gun after the incident. Li's wife, Li's sister Shunbao, and village police officer Ji A'quan were unable to escape and were arrested by police officers dispatched by the County Public Security Bureau and sent to the court. Chief Prosecutor Zhang Bing severely interrogated Li's wife and learned that the criminals had fled to Pinghu. Li's wife and the village police officer were ordered to be detained. Li's sister Shunbao was temporarily released on bail. After receiving the news, Sun Minze, the head of the Baochong Tuan, telegraphed the Pinghu Security Corps to order them to investigate the whereabouts of the criminals and detain them at any time. In the afternoon, the two criminals were found in Donghu carrying guns and the symbol of the county's security corps. They were immediately detained and temporarily held in the headquarters, awaiting the court's arrival for interrogation.

Changshu: Villagers Report Famine in Succession

There is a severe drought here. Forty percent of the fields in the county have not been planted, and those that have been transplanted are also withered. According to general estimates, the future autumn harvest will be no more than 30 to 40 percent. The county government is now doing its best to save the situation. As for drinking water, the rivers in the urban area are mostly dry. Many Buddhist grandmothers are prostrating themselves on the riverbed to pray. 107 of the public wells in the urban and rural areas have dried up. The district office is investigating and trying to dig deeper to temporarily provide drinking water. However, the weather has been hot for days, and there is still no sign of rain, making people even more apprehensive. Farmers from various villages have reported the famine and petitioned the county government, party headquarters, farmers' association, and other places. However, the authorities can only try to comfort them and urge them to return to their villages to cultivate. On the morning of the 15th, County Magistrate and District Chief Shen Changjun, along with Assistant Zhou Zimei and others, went to various villages in Da Yi Bridge to inspect the disaster situation.

Nantong: Drawing River Water to Relieve Drought

Tong County has suffered from a long drought, resulting in disaster. People from all walks of life in the area have been meeting for days to discuss relief measures and have decided to build a dam at Ren Harbor and use an electric engine to draw river water for internal irrigation. The funds needed will be allocated from the county's construction funds. An engineer has been hired to expedite the process.

Notice of Inspection for the Hai Customs Police

The Hai Customs Police stationed in Tongruhai are ordered to undergo an inspection by the Ministry of Finance and to examine the shooting skills of the police officers. Live ammunition shooting will be held on the 16th in Lvsi and Juegang, on the 17th in Juzhen and Liujia Fangong Embankment, on the 18th in Dongyu Town and Haimen Public Stadium, on the 19th in Sanyu Town, and on the 20th at Jianshan in Nantong.

Xiaoshan: Soaring Rice Prices Amidst Severe Drought

The water in the Xiaoshan city river has dried up, and ships have stopped traveling. The Shaoxiao Night Navigation and Yue'an companies' commercial ships will also be suspended, greatly hindering transportation. As a result, the rice market in the urban area has risen sharply. On the 15th, the price of rice suddenly increased by 1.2 yuan. Top-quality white late rice is 9.6 yuan, second-quality late rice is also 9.4 yuan, and even the starting price is 8.6 yuan. The general laborers are crying out in misery because of the soaring rice prices.

Haimen: Disaster Prevention and Epidemic Prevention Conference

The county government held a disaster prevention and epidemic prevention conference yesterday morning and resolved the following measures: (1) The districts will investigate the food surplus and deficit of each household, accurately collect statistics, and submit them for overall relief. (2) A letter will be sent to the Food Management Committee to quickly accumulate 5,000 dan of wheat for famine relief. (3) The county government will issue a notice strictly prohibiting the export of miscellaneous grains and will task the heads of districts and townships with effectively stopping it. (4) The Agricultural Extension Institute will be instructed to formulate replanting methods and prepare drought-resistant seeds for distribution as loans. (5) The districts will be instructed to remove fish weirs and various obstacles in the river to ensure smooth water flow. (6) The Chamber of Commerce will be instructed to order grain merchants not to hoard and raise prices. Violators will be prosecuted and punished. (7) The Finance Department will be petitioned to approve the allocation of 1,000 yuan from the local reserve fund for epidemic prevention expenses. The Public Security Bureau will be instructed to convene Chinese and Western medical associations to discuss epidemic prevention methods and implement them effectively.
